r3553 | vasiljevic | 2014-02-18 19:43:29 +0100 (Tue, 18 Feb 2014) | 9 lines

Graph editor: improvements related to box content editing

When you are editing box content and you have made some changes:
- if you click on the graph background, changes will be stored in the appropriate box(es) and all boxes will be deselected
- if you click on a box, changes will be  stored in the appropriate box(es) and the clicked box will be selected without altering transitions; so, you can just click on the next box you want to edit (if you don't make any changes in selected box content, the Graph editor will behave as usual: it will draw/remove transitions)
- if you do "Save" or "Save as", changes will be stored in the appropriate box(es) before saving
- in the all previous cases if there is an error in the box content, the operation will be canceled and you go back to the edit field, to fix the error
- if you want to cancel editing, just hit ESC

r806 | paumier | 2009-05-12 10:59:13 +0200 (Tue, 12 May 2009) | 1 line

Bounds computation is adapted to the new .tfst format that deals with Korean
------------------------------------------------------------------------
r792 | paumier | 2009-05-05 11:48:51 +0200 (Tue, 05 May 2009) | 1 line

Format .tfst has been modified in order to handle the notion of logical letter that is useful for Korean. Now, start and end offsets are represented by x.y.z where x is the position in tokens, y the position in characters in the current token and z is the position in logical letters in the current character. For Korean, it is useful to know that we are at n logical letters inside a syllabic character. For any other language, this last value should always be 0.
------------------------------------------------------------------------

This version uses libUnitexJNI.so built from separate static libraries (Unitex vs UFO's virtual file system).
------------------------------------------------------------------------
r373 | surcin@kwaga.com | 2009-04-23 10:13:42 +0200 (Thu, 23 Apr 2009) | 4 lines

This project links static libraries UnitexCore and UnitexVirtual (UFO) and adds a JNI interface. It produces libUnitexJNI.so to be put into Pulse/lib directory.

To be built, this project needs UnitexCoreStatic project to be present in the workspace.

All unitary Tests Ok
------------------------------------------------------------------------
r294 | laval@kwaga.com | 2009-04-15 17:11:26 +0200 (Wed, 15 Apr 2009) | 1 line

mailProcess.t really send a mail to doe@kwaga.com
------------------------------------------------------------------------
r293 | surcin@kwaga.com | 2009-04-15 15:48:53 +0200 (Wed, 15 Apr 2009) | 23 lines

1) Input files

Use parameters in MailItemCollectionReader.xml:
 - InputDirectory: specify the path to the input directory where mails are stored as *.xml 
 - InputUrl: (optional) specify the URL where to fetch the *.xml input files (if not empty
	this parameter preempts InputDirectory)
 - Encoding: currently ISO-8859-1
 - Language: currently not in use (always French)

In case we process local files, the input files are renamed appending ".processing" while
they are being processed, and renamed with suffix ".done" when finished.

2) Output files

Use paremeters in XmiWriterCasConsumer.xml:
 - OutputDirectory: (mandatory) the path to the output directory
 - OutputURL: (optional) the URL where to post the output files

When the local output files are complete, a semaphore file with the same name and
ending with ".ok" is generated.

If the OutputURL parameter is not empty, the output file is posted to this URL.

The integration of Unitex through JNI is now fully operational.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
r207 | surcin@kwaga.com | 2009-03-27 13:44:03 +0100 (Fri, 27 Mar 2009) | 14 lines

Major refactoring.

1. Aggregation

Put all processing chain into a single aggregated annotator (AggregateChain.xml)

The MailItmCollectionReader now just reads the files, but the XML interpretation is done by a new KwagaMailDocumentAnnotator. This way, the whole chain can be tested in the CAS Visual Debugger.

2. JNI

Introduction of JNI linking to Unitex library in JUnitex class. So far there are still some problems (corrupt memory) from time to time. And we must resolve the problem of where to load the library from (loadLibrary doesn't work as expected).

Stay put.

Refactoring projet

r147 | surcin@kwaga.com | 2009-03-20 11:35:00 +0100 (Fri, 20 Mar 2009) | 8 lines

First functional version of the processing chain!

MailItemCollectionReader reads the xml mail dumps.
RegExAnnotator looks for email addresses and urls using regexps.
DynamicDictionaryAnnotator transform them into Unitex DELAF dictionaries.
UnitexAnnotator wraps calls to native Unitex and turn the output of the transducers into document annotations of type "Category".

So far the CAS consumer is the default XMI dumper.
------------------------------------------------------------------------

r137 | surcin@kwaga.com | 2009-03-19 15:32:38 +0100 (Thu, 19 Mar 2009) | 1 line

Initial version without unnecessary files and folders.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
r136 | surcin@kwaga.com | 2009-03-19 15:29:49 +0100 (Thu, 19 Mar 2009) | 8 lines

Initial import.

Simple CPE architecture with:
- MailItemCollectionReader: reads XML mail dumps, the mail body text will become the CAS document text, and all other nodes become document annotations;
- RegExAnnotator: reused from UIMA sandbox, with a concept file allowing to recognize email addresses and URLs;
- DynamicDictionaryAnnotator: takes the recognized emails and urls and create a dynamic dictionary for all emails and one for all urls using DELAF format;
- UnitexAnnotator: wraps the calls to the native Unitex

------------------------------------------------------------------------
